			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Wells Fargo (disambiguation)">Wells Fargo (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Wells Fargo &amp; Company</b> is an American multinational <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> company headquartered in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco, California</a>, with central offices throughout the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Wells-Fargo-&amp;-Company-Feb-2009-10-K_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells-Fargo-&amp;-Company-Feb-2009-10-K-10">[10]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks" title="List of largest banks">world's fourth-largest bank</a> by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest banks in the United States">fourth largest bank in the US</a> by total assets.<sup id="cite_ref-BankCap_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BankCap-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune-12">[12]</a></sup> Wells Fargo is ranked number 26 on the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest US corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In July 2015, Wells Fargo became the world's largest bank by market capitalization, edging past <a href="/wiki/ICBC" class="mw-redirect" title="ICBC">ICBC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune-12">[12]</a></sup> before slipping behind <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a> in September 2016, in the wake of a scandal involving the creation of over <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_account_fraud_scandal" title="Wells Fargo account fraud scandal">2 million fake bank accounts</a>  and illegal manipulation of other accounts by Wells Fargo employees.<sup id="cite_ref-BankCap_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BankCap-11">[11]</a></sup> Wells Fargo fell behind <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> to third by bank deposits in 2017<sup id="cite_ref-WellsFargoMidwestClosures2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WellsFargoMidwestClosures2-14">[14]</a></sup> and behind <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> to fourth by total assets in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Wells Fargo is incorporated in Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Wells Fargo &amp; Company</caption><tbody><tr><td data-file-height="1306"></a><div>Wells Fargo's headquarters complex in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Berkeley_Wells_Fargo.jpg/220px-Berkeley_Wells_Fargo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="602"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berkeley_Wells_Fargo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wells Fargo <a href="/wiki/Branch_(banking)" title="Branch (banking)">branch</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">Berkeley, California</a></div></div></div>
<p>The firm's primary operating subsidiary is <a href="/wiki/National_bank" title="National bank">national bank</a> <b>Wells Fargo Bank, N.A.</b>, which designates its main office as <a href="/wiki/Sioux_Falls,_South_Dakota" title="Sioux Falls, South Dakota">Sioux Falls, South Dakota</a>. Wells Fargo in its present form is a result of a merger between San Francisco–based Wells Fargo &amp; Company and <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Norwest_Corporation" title="Norwest Corporation">Norwest Corporation</a> in 1998 and the subsequent 2008 acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a>. Following the mergers, the company transferred its headquarters to Wells Fargo's headquarters in San Francisco and merged its operating subsidiary with Wells Fargo's operating subsidiary in Sioux Falls. Along with JPMorgan Chase, Bank of America, and Citigroup, Wells Fargo is one of the "<a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(banking)#United_States" title="Big Four (banking)">Big Four Banks</a>" of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> As of June 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it had 8,050 <a href="/wiki/Branches" class="mw-redirect" title="Branches">branches</a> and 13,000 <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machines" class="mw-redirect" title="Automated teller machines">ATMs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WF_Quarterly_Fact_Sheet_2Q2018_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WF_Quarterly_Fact_Sheet_2Q2018-3">[3]</a></sup> In 2018 the company had operations in 35 countries with over 70 million customers globally.<sup id="cite_ref-WF_Quarterly_Fact_Sheet_2Q2018_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WF_Quarterly_Fact_Sheet_2Q2018-3">[3]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2014, Wells Fargo was named the world's most valuable bank brand for the second consecutive year<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Banker" title="The Banker">The Banker</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Brand_Finance" title="Brand Finance">Brand Finance</a> study of the top 500 banking brands.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 2016, Wells Fargo ranked 7th on the <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes (magazine)">Forbes</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Global 2000</a> list of largest public companies in the world and ranked 27th on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest companies in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-wellsfargotoday_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wellsfargotoday-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2015, the company was ranked the 22nd most admired company in the world, and the 7th most respected company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-wellsfargotoday_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wellsfargotoday-8">[8]</a></sup> As of December 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the company had a <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poors" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard &amp; Poors">Standard &amp; Poors</a> <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> of A−.<sup id="cite_ref-Credit_ratings_Q32018_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Credit_ratings_Q32018-9">[9]</a></sup> However, for a brief period in 2007, the company was the only AAA‑rated bank, reflecting the highest credit rating from two firms.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>On February 2, 2018, the <a href="/wiki/US_Federal_Reserve_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="US Federal Reserve Bank">US Federal Reserve Bank</a> barred Wells Fargo from growing its nearly <a href="/wiki/US%24" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>2 trillion-asset base any further, <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_account_fraud_scandal" title="Wells Fargo account fraud scandal">based upon years of misconduct</a>, until Wells Fargo fixes its internal problems to the satisfaction of the Federal Reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In April 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported that the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Labor" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Labor">US Department of Labor</a> had launched a probe into whether Wells Fargo was pushing its customers into more expensive <a href="/wiki/Retirement_plans_in_the_United_States" title="Retirement plans in the United States">retirement plans</a> as well as into <a href="/wiki/Retirement_fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Retirement fund">retirement funds</a> managed by Wells Fargo itself.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Subsequently in May 2018, <i>The Wall Street Journal</i> reported that Wells Fargo's business banking group had improperly altered documents about business clients in 2017 and early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In June 2018, Wells Fargo began retreating from <a href="/wiki/Retail_banking" title="Retail banking">retail banking</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a> by announcing the sale of all its physical bank branch locations in <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> to <a href="/wiki/Flagstar_Bank" title="Flagstar Bank">Flagstar Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WellsFargoMidwestClosures2_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WellsFargoMidwestClosures2-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WellsFargoMidwestClosures1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WellsFargoMidwestClosures1-26">[26]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Wells_Fargo" title="History of Wells Fargo">History of Wells Fargo</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wells_Fargo_History_Museums">Wells Fargo History Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Wells Fargo History Museums" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company operates 12 museums, most known as a <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_History_Museum" title="Wells Fargo History Museum">Wells Fargo History Museum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> in its corporate buildings in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Denver,_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver, Colorado">Denver, Colorado</a>; <a href="/wiki/Des_Moines,_Iowa" title="Des Moines, Iowa">Des Moines, Iowa</a>; <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a>; <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a>; <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia, Pennsylvania</a>; <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>; <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento, California</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a>. Displays include original <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach" title="Stagecoach">stagecoaches</a>, photographs, gold nuggets and mining artifacts, the Pony Express, <a href="/wiki/Telegraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Telegraph">telegraph</a> equipment and historic bank artifacts. The company also operates a museum about company history in the <a href="/wiki/Pony_Express_Terminal" title="Pony Express Terminal">Pony Express Terminal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park" title="Old Sacramento State Historic Park">Old Sacramento State Historic Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento, California</a>, which was the company's second office,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and the Wells Fargo History Museum in <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_San_Diego_State_Historic_Park" title="Old Town San Diego State Historic Park">Old Town San Diego State Historic Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego, California">San Diego, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>Wells Fargo operates the Alaska Heritage Museum in <a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage, Alaska</a>, which features a large collection of Alaskan Native artifacts, <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a> carvings and baskets, fine art by Alaskan artists, and displays about Wells Fargo history in the <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Gold_Rush" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaskan Gold Rush">Alaskan Gold Rush</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_dates">Key dates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Key dates" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG/220px-WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG/220px-WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WellsFargoChinatownHoustonnew.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wells Fargo bank in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Houston" title="Chinatown, Houston">Chinatown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth,_TX.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png/220px-Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1941" data-file-height="1251"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 142px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png/220px-Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="142" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_in_Fort_Worth,_TX.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A remodeled Wells Fargo bank in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a></div></div></div> 
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo,_TX_IMG_1054.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo%2C_TX_IMG_1054.JPG/220px-Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo%2C_TX_IMG_1054.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo%2C_TX_IMG_1054.JPG/220px-Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo%2C_TX_IMG_1054.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_in_Laredo,_TX_IMG_1054.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wells Fargo in <a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Texas" title="Laredo, Texas">Laredo</a>, Texas</div></div></div>
<ul><li>1852: <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wells" title="Henry Wells">Henry Wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Fargo" title="William Fargo">William G. Fargo</a>, the two founders of <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a>, formed Wells Fargo &amp; Company to provide express and banking services to California.</li>
<li>1860: Wells Fargo gained control of <a href="/wiki/Butterfield_Overland_Mail" title="Butterfield Overland Mail">Butterfield Overland Mail</a> Company, leading to operation of the western portion of the <a href="/wiki/Pony_Express" title="Pony Express">Pony Express</a>.</li>
<li>1866: "Grand consolidation" united Wells Fargo, Holladay, and Overland Mail stage lines under the Wells Fargo name.</li>
<li>1872: <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Tevis" title="Lloyd Tevis">Lloyd Tevis</a>, a friend of the Central Pacific "Big Four" and holder of rights to operate an express service over the <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcontinental Railroad">Transcontinental Railroad</a>, acquires control of the company.</li>
<li>1905: Wells Fargo separated its banking and express operations; Wells Fargo's bank was merged with the Nevada National Bank to form the Wells Fargo Nevada National Bank.</li>
<li>1918: As a wartime measure, the <a href="/wiki/US_Federal_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="US Federal Government">US Federal Government</a> nationalized Wells Fargo's express franchise into a <a href="/wiki/Federal_agencies_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal agencies of the United States">federal agency</a> known as the US <a href="/wiki/Railway_Express_Agency" title="Railway Express Agency">Railway Express Agency</a>. The US Federal Government took control of the express company. The bank began rebuilding but with a focus on commercial markets. After the war, REA was privatized and continued service until 1975.</li>
<li>1923: Wells Fargo Nevada merged with the Union Trust Company to form the Wells Fargo Bank &amp; Union Trust Company.</li>
<li>1929: Northwest Bancorporation was formed as a banking association.</li>
<li>1954: Wells Fargo &amp; Union Trust shortened its name to Wells Fargo Bank.</li>
<li>1960: Wells Fargo merged with American Trust Company to form the Wells Fargo Bank American Trust Company.</li>
<li>1962: Wells Fargo American Trust again shortened its name to Wells Fargo Bank.</li>
<li>1968: Wells Fargo converted to a federal banking charter, becoming Wells Fargo Bank, N.A. Wells Fargo merged with Henry Trione's Sonoma Mortgage in a $10.8 million stock transfer, making Trione the largest shareholder in Wells Fargo until Warren Buffett and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Annenberg" title="Walter Annenberg">Walter Annenberg</a> later surpassed him.<sup id="cite_ref-trione_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trione-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>1969: Wells Fargo &amp; Company holding company was formed, with Wells Fargo Bank as its main subsidiary.</li>
<li>1982: Northwest Bancorporation acquired consumer finance firm Dial Finance which is renamed Norwest Financial Service the following year.</li>
<li>1983: Northwest Bancorporation was renamed <a href="/wiki/Norwest_Corporation" title="Norwest Corporation">Norwest Corporation</a>.</li>
<li>1983: <a href="/wiki/White_Eagle_(robbery)" class="mw-redirect" title="White Eagle (robbery)">White Eagle</a>, largest US bank heist to date took place at a Wells Fargo depot in <a href="/wiki/West_Hartford,_Connecticut" title="West Hartford, Connecticut">West Hartford, Connecticut</a>.</li>
<li>1986: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/Crocker_National_Bank" title="Crocker National Bank">Crocker National Corporation</a> from <a href="/wiki/Midland_Bank" title="Midland Bank">Midland Bank</a>.</li>
<li>1987: Wells Fargo acquired the personal trust business of <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>.</li>
<li>1988: Wells Fargo acquired Barclays Bank of California from <a href="/wiki/Barclays_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Barclays plc">Barclays plc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>1995: Wells Fargo became the first major US financial services firm to offer Internet banking.</li>
<li>1996: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/First_Interstate_Bancorp" title="First Interstate Bancorp">First Interstate Bancorp</a> for US$11.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>1998: Wells Fargo Bank was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Norwest_Corporation" title="Norwest Corporation">Norwest Corporation</a> of Minneapolis.<sup id="cite_ref-Wells_Fargo_and_Norwest_to_Merge_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells_Fargo_and_Norwest_to_Merge-34">[34]</a></sup>  (Norwest was the surviving company; however, it chose to continue business under the more well-known Wells Fargo name.)</li>
<li>2000: Wells Fargo Bank acquired <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Alaska" title="National Bank of Alaska">National Bank of Alaska</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>2000: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/First_Security_Corporation" title="First Security Corporation">First Security Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wells_Fargo_and_Norwest_to_Merge_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells_Fargo_and_Norwest_to_Merge-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>2001: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/H.D._Vest_Financial_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="H.D. Vest Financial Services">H.D. Vest Financial Services</a> for US$128 million, but sold it in 2015 for US$580 million.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>2007: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/CIT_Group" title="CIT Group">CIT</a>'s construction unit.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>2007: Wells Fargo acquired Placer Sierra Bank.</li>
<li>2007: Wells Fargo acquired Greater Bay Bancorp, which had US$7.4 billion in assets, in a US$1.5 billion transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>2008: Wells Fargo acquired United Bancorporation of Wyoming.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>2008: Wells Fargo acquired Century Bancshares of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>2008: Wells Fargo acquired <a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a> Corporation.</li>
<li>2009: Wells Fargo acquired North Coast Surety Insurance Services.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>2012: Wells Fargo acquired Merlin Securities.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>2012: Wells Fargo acquired stake in The Rock Creek Group LP.</li>
<li>2019: CEO Tim Sloan resigns causing stock to jump and leaves General Counsel <a href="/wiki/C._Allen_Parker" title="C. Allen Parker">C. Allen Parker</a> as Interim CEO. On September 27, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Scharf" title="Charles Scharf">Charles Scharf</a> is announced as the firm's new CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-Sun_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sun-45">[45]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wachovia_acquisition">Wachovia acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Wachovia acquisition" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg/220px-2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3678" data-file-height="2452"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg/220px-2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-11-22_Wells_Fargo_ATMs_lit_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A former Wachovia branch converted to Wells Fargo in the fall of 2011 in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham, North Carolina</a></div></div></div>
<p>On October 3, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a> agreed to be bought by Wells Fargo for about US$14.8 billion in an all-stock transaction. This news came four days after the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a> (FDIC) made moves to have <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> buy Wachovia for US$2.1 billion. Citigroup protested Wachovia's agreement to sell itself to Wells Fargo and threatened legal action over the matter. However, the deal with Wells Fargo overwhelmingly won shareholder approval since it valued Wachovia at about seven times what Citigroup offered. To further ensure shareholder approval, Wachovia issued Wells Fargo preferred stock that holds 39.9% of the voting power in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>On October 4, 2008, a New York state judge issued a temporary injunction blocking the transaction from going forward while the situation was sorted out.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Citigroup alleged that they had an exclusivity agreement with Wachovia that barred Wachovia from negotiating with other potential buyers. The injunction was overturned late in the evening on October 5, 2008, by New York state appeals court.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Citigroup and Wells Fargo then entered into negotiations brokered by the FDIC to reach an amicable solution to the impasse. Those negotiations failed. Sources say that Citigroup was unwilling to take on more risk than the US$42 billion that would have been the cap under the previous FDIC-backed deal (with the FDIC incurring all losses over US$42 billion). Citigroup did not block the merger, but indicated they would seek damages of US$60 billion for breach of an alleged exclusivity agreement with Wachovia.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_by_US_Treasury_Department_during_2008_financial_crisis">Investment by US Treasury Department during 2008 financial crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Investment by US Treasury Department during 2008 financial crisis" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On October 28, 2008, Wells Fargo was the recipient of US$25 billion of Emergency Economic Stabilization Act funds in the form of a preferred stock purchase by the <a href="/wiki/US_Treasury_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US Treasury Department">US Treasury Department</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Tests by the US Federal Government revealed that Wells Fargo needed an additional US$13.7 billion in order to remain well capitalized if the economy were to deteriorate further under stress test scenarios. On May 11, 2009, Wells Fargo announced an additional stock offering which was completed on May 13, 2009, raising US$8.6 billion in capital. The remaining US$4.9 billion in capital was planned to be raised through earnings. On Dec. 23, 2009, Wells Fargo redeemed the US$25 billion of preferred stock issued to the US Treasury. As part of the redemption of the preferred stock, Wells Fargo also paid accrued dividends of US$131.9 million, bringing the total dividends paid to US$1.441 billion since the preferred stock was issued in October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_Wells_Fargo_Securities">History of Wells Fargo Securities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History of Wells Fargo Securities" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Wells Fargo Securities was established in 2009 to house Wells Fargo's capital markets group which it obtained during the Wachovia acquisition. Prior to that point, Wells Fargo had little to no participation in investment banking activities, though Wachovia had a well established investment banking practice which it operated under the <a href="/wiki/Wachovia_Securities" title="Wachovia Securities">Wachovia Securities</a> banner.
</p><p>Wachovia's institutional capital markets and investment banking business arose from the merger of Wachovia and First Union. First Union had bought <a href="/wiki/Bowles_Hollowell_Connor_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Bowles Hollowell Connor &amp; Co.">Bowles Hollowell Connor &amp; Co.</a> on April 30, 1998 adding to its <a href="/wiki/Merger_and_acquisition" class="mw-redirect" title="Merger and acquisition">merger and acquisition</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_yield" class="mw-redirect" title="High yield">high yield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leveraged_finance" class="mw-redirect" title="Leveraged finance">leveraged finance</a>, equity underwriting, <a href="/wiki/Private_placement" title="Private placement">private placement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loan_syndication" class="mw-redirect" title="Loan syndication">loan syndication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_finance" title="Public finance">public finance</a> capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>Legacy components of Wells Fargo Securities include <a href="/wiki/Wachovia_Securities" title="Wachovia Securities">Wachovia Securities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowles_Hollowell_Connor_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Bowles Hollowell Connor &amp; Co.">Bowles Hollowell Connor &amp; Co.</a>, Barrington Associates, <a href="/wiki/Halsey,_Stuart_%26_Co." title="Halsey, Stuart &amp; Co.">Halsey, Stuart &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bache_%26_Co." title="Bache &amp; Co.">Leopold Cahn &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bache_%26_Co." title="Bache &amp; Co.">Bache &amp; Co.</a>. <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Securities" title="Prudential Securities">Prudential Securities</a>, <a href="/wiki/A.G._Edwards,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="A.G. Edwards, Inc.">A.G. Edwards, Inc.</a> and the investment banking arm of <a href="/wiki/Citadel_LLC" title="Citadel LLC">Citadel LLC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg/170px-Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="399" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="1477"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 399px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg/170px-Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="399" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Duke_Energy_Center_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Duke_Energy_Center" title="Duke Energy Center">Duke Energy Center</a> in Charlotte, North Carolina home of Wells Fargo Securities<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, Wells Fargo ranked #1 among banks and insurance companies, and #13 overall, in <a href="/wiki/Newsweek_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Newsweek Magazine">Newsweek Magazine</a>'s inaugural "Green Rankings" of the country's 500 largest companies.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 2013, the company was recognized by the EPA Center for Corporate Climate Leadership as a Climate Leadership Award winner, in the category "Excellence in Greenhouse Gas Management (Goal Setting Certificate)"; this recognition was for the company's aim to reduce its absolute <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> from its US operations by 35% by 2020 versus 2008 levels.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Wells Fargo had provided more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6 billion</span> in financing for environmentally beneficial business opportunities, including supporting 185 commercial-scale solar photovoltaic projects and 27 utility-scale wind projects nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2018)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Wells Fargo has launched what it believes to be the first blog among its industry peers to report on its environmental stewardship and to solicit feedback and ideas from its stakeholders.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire:_Wells_Fargo_Launches_Environmental_Stewardship_Blog_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire:_Wells_Fargo_Launches_Environmental_Stewardship_Blog-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"We want to be as open and clear as possible about our environmental efforts – both our accomplishments and challenges – and share our experiences, ideas and thoughts as we work to integrate environmental responsibility into everything we do," said Mary Wenzel, director of Environmental Affairs. "We also want to hear and learn from our customers. By working together, we can do even more to protect and preserve natural resources for future generations."</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Mary Wenzel, director of Environmental Affairs, Wells Fargo, 2010 press release</cite></div></blockquote>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations_and_services">Operations and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operations and services" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_footprint.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wells_Fargo_footprint.png/220px-Wells_Fargo_footprint.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5758" data-file-height="3000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 115px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wells_Fargo_footprint.png/220px-Wells_Fargo_footprint.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="115" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_footprint.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Wells Fargo branches in August 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Wells Fargo delineates three different business segments when reporting results: <a href="/wiki/Retail_banking" title="Retail banking">Community Banking</a>; <a href="/wiki/Wholesale_Banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Wholesale Banking">Wholesale Banking</a>; and Wealth, Brokerage and Retirement.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_banking">Community banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Community banking" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Community Banking segment includes Regional Banking, Diversified Products, and Consumer Deposits groups, as well as Wells Fargo Customer Connection (formerly Wells Fargo Phone Bank, Wachovia Direct Access, the National Business Banking Center, and Credit Card Customer Service). Wells Fargo also has around 2,000 stand-alone mortgage branches throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> There are mini-branches located inside of other buildings, which are almost exclusively grocery stores, that usually contain ATMs, basic <a href="/wiki/Bank_teller" title="Bank teller">teller</a> services, and, space permitting, an office for private meetings with customers.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In March 2017, Wells Fargo announced a plan to offer smartphone-based transactions with mobile wallets including Wells Fargo Wallet, Android Pay and Samsung Pay.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_lending">Consumer lending</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Consumer lending" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>As of Q3 2011, Wells Fargo Home Mortgage was the largest retail mortgage lender in the United States, originating one out of every four home loans.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Wells Fargo services US$1.8 trillion in home mortgages, the second largest servicing portfolio in the US<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> It was reported in 2012 Wells Fargo reached 30% market share for US mortgages, however, the then-CEO <a href="/wiki/John_Stumpf" title="John Stumpf">John Stumpf</a> had said the numbers were misleading because about half of that share represented the aggregation of smaller loans that were then sold on the secondary market. In 2013, its share was closer to 22%; of which eight percentage points was aggregation.<sup id="cite_ref-euromoney1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euromoney1-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wells_Fargo_private_student_loans">Wells Fargo private student loans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Wells Fargo private student loans" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Wells Fargo private student loans are available to students to pay for college expenses, such as tuition, books, computers, or housing.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Loans are available for <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a>, career and <a href="/wiki/Community_colleges" class="mw-redirect" title="Community colleges">community colleges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate school</a>, law school and medical school. Wells Fargo also provides private student loan consolidation and student loans for parents.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment_lending">Equipment lending</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Equipment lending" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Wells Fargo has various divisions that finance and lease equipment to different types of companies.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> One venture is <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Rail" title="Wells Fargo Rail">Wells Fargo Rail</a>, which in 2015 agreed to the purchase of <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital_Rail_Services" title="GE Capital Rail Services">GE Capital Rail Services</a> and merged in with <a href="/wiki/First_Union_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="First Union Rail">First Union Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In late 2015, it was announced that Wells Fargo would buy three GE units focused on business loans equipment financing.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth_and_Investment_Management">Wealth and Investment Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Wealth and Investment Management" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg/170px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3276"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 113px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg/170px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="113" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Advisors_headguarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wells Fargo Advisors headquarters in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, Missouri</div></div></div>
<p>Wells Fargo offers investment products through its subsidiaries, Wells Fargo Investments, LLC and Wells Fargo Advisors, LLC, as well as through national broker/dealer firms. The company also serves high-net-worth individuals through its <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">private bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wealth_management" title="Wealth management">family wealth</a> group.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg/220px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="494" data-file-height="202"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 90px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg/220px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="90" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg/330px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg/440px-Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Advisors.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo for Wells Fargo Advisors</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Advisors" title="Wells Fargo Advisors">Wells Fargo Advisors</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Brokerage" class="mw-redirect" title="Brokerage">brokerage</a> subsidiary of Wells Fargo, located in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, Missouri. It is the third largest brokerage firm in the United States as of the third quarter of 2010 with US$1.1 trillion retail client assets under management.<sup id="cite_ref-wellsfargotoday_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wellsfargotoday-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>Wells Fargo Advisors was known as <a href="/wiki/Wachovia_Securities" title="Wachovia Securities">Wachovia Securities</a> until May 1, 2009, when it legally changed names following the Wells Fargo's acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Wachovia_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Wachovia Corporation">Wachovia Corporation</a>.
</p><p>In September 2018, Wells Fargo announced to cut 26,450 jobs by 2020 to reduce costs by US$4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wells_Fargo_Asset_Management">Wells Fargo Asset Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Wells Fargo Asset Management" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>

<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wells_Fargo_Securities">Wells Fargo Securities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wells_Fargo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Wells Fargo Securities" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Wells Fargo Securities, LLC</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="logo" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Securities_Logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="Wells Fargo Securities Logo.svg"
